4 PREDICTION AND EVALUATION OF ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACTS OF THE PROJECT
4.1 Introduction
In accordance with the provisions of the Supreme Decree D.S. N°40/2012, article 18 letter f),
modified by D.S. 30/2023, both from the Ministry of the Environment (MMA), as part of
the contents of an Environmental Impact Study, “a prediction and
evaluation of the environmental impact of the project or activity. Impact prediction will consist of
the identification and estimation or quantification of direct and indirect alterations to the elements
of the environment described in the baseline, derived from the execution or modification of the
project or activity for each of its phases.” In this way, this Chapter presents the
prediction and evaluation of environmental impacts derived from parts, actions and physical works
of the “Mining Development Project for the Extraction of Clays for the Production of Concentrated
Rare Earths” (hereinafter, the Project), in its construction, operation and closure phases.
For the prediction and evaluation of impacts, the general definitions and criteria have been applied.
established in the document “Evaluation Criteria in the SEIA: Scope and principles
methodological for the evaluation of environmental impacts” (SEA, 2023). In this way, the
This Chapter is structured as follows:
Item 4.2 includes the Prediction of the environmental impacts of the Project, defined as the
identification and estimation or quantification of direct alterations to the elements of the Environment
Environment described in the Baseline, derived from the execution of the Project, for each of
its phases.
Item 4.3 presents the Evaluation of the environmental impacts of the Project which, according to
to literal f) of article 18 of the SEIA Regulations, consists of determining whether the impacts
predicted may constitute significant impacts based on the criteria of Article 11 of
Law 19,300 and specified in Title II of the SEIA Regulations.
For the evaluation of impacts, a qualitative methodology is used, using as a theoretical basis
the proposal of Conesa Fernández (1997) and the professional experience of the multidisciplinary team
in charge of preparing the EIA, supported, in the case of certain components, by an analysis
quantitative, based on models, simulations and mathematical calculations, in the most
unfavorable. When, due to its nature, an impact cannot be quantified, its prediction only
will have a qualitative character; This, in accordance with the provisions of article 18, letter f, of the
SEIA Regulations.
4-1
==================================================================================
PAGE 11
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
The detailed description of those effects, characteristics and circumstances of article 11 of
Law No. 19,300 are presented in Chapter 5 of this EIA. In case it is predicted and evaluated
a significant adverse impact, a Measures Plan is incorporated in Chapter 7 of this EIA
of Mitigation, Repair and/or Compensation, as appropriate, proposed with the purpose of
avoid or reduce adverse effects.
4.
2 Prediction of environmental impacts
4.2.1 Identification of Environmental Impacts
Identification of environmental impacts is understood as the recognition of these, derived from the
execution or modification of the Project or activity that is subject to environmental evaluation. Of
in accordance with the guidelines and criteria established in the document “Evaluation criteria in the
SEIA: Scope and methodological principles for the evaluation of environmental impacts” (SEA,
2023) the following must be taken into consideration:
a) Identification of impact generating factors (FGI)
The FGI are those elements of the Project, in consideration of their location and temporality, as well as
such as its emissions, effluents, waste, exploitation, extraction, use or intervention of resources
natural resources, labor, supplies or basic inputs and products or services generated, according to
appropriate, that by themselves, generate alteration in the environment and that are identifiable
in each of the phases of the Project.
b) The identification of impacts must consider the alterations to the elements of the
environment.
c) Application of cause-effect matrix methodology.
For the application of this methodology, the following guidelines and criteria are considered:
• Determine and list the FGI, grouping them in the different phases of the Project or activity,
such as the construction, operation or closure phase, if applicable.
• Identify and list the elements of the environment that can potentially be
affected by the FGI of the Project or activity. It is recommended that, in a first analysis,
consider all elements of the environment (protection objects and attributes) with
the purpose of ensuring that the analysis has been carried out on them.
• Cross both lists (FGI with the elements of the environment) and mark the
intersections (boxes) where the Project or activity is expected to generate some
alteration to the environment.
4-2
==================================================================================
PAGE 12
==================================================================================
Chapter 4

Rare Earth Concentrate
d) Relationship of each of the alterations to the environment identified with the effects,
characteristics and circumstances of article 11 of the Law.
e) The identification of the impact must be analyzed in light of the evaluation of the effects
synergistic and cumulative impacts.
Next, the identification of impacts is developed, considering the above.
previously.
4.2.1.1 Identification of parts, works and actions of the Project
The “Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for the Production of Concentrated
Rare Earths” consists of the construction and operation of a mining site and a
processing of clays, a material present in the area, which due to natural effects is found
highly weathered, with the presence of lanthanides absorbed in clay minerals.
The plant has a capacity to process up to 320 tons/hour of Earth concentrate
Rare. The Project considers three clay extraction zones (ZE Victoria Norte, ZE Luna, ZE
Maite), a disposal area for waste and processed clays (ZD Neptuno), a
topsoil collection (ZAV), a clay processing plant and a stockpile for collection
temporary material prior to processing, a power line and its existing connection and the
construction of internal roads to access different areas. Furthermore, it is considered the
construction (relocation) of an existing oil pipeline (Hualpén – San Fernando), owned by
ENAP, reason for the exploitation of the Maite ZE. The project in turn has the implementation
of temporary works corresponding to work facilities, for the construction and qualification
of the Project works.
The main works and facilities of the project are presented in Table 4-1. In Chapter 1.
Description of the EIA Project, greater detail is presented about its parts, works and actions of the
Project.

4.2.1.5 Estimation or quantification of environmental impacts
The impact evaluation methodology considers a qualitative analysis for all those
environmental components susceptible to being altered5 in such a way as to identify
preliminarily the possible impacts. After said identification, it is presented for each
component an evaluation, equally qualitative, based on the expert judgment of the team
multidisciplinary team responsible for preparing the EIA, supported, when appropriate, by a
predictive model and/or numerical or quantitative analysis. This, considering the condition most
unfavorable from the environmental point of view, as established in Article 18 letter f of the
SEIA Regulations. By virtue of the above, this EIA contemplated the development of the
following analyzes through predictive models:
- Meteorological and dispersion modeling of atmospheric pollutants
- Noise and Vibration Study
- Road impact study
- Soil erosion map
- Photomontage
4.3 Environmental Impact Assessment of the Project
Subparagraph f) of article 18 of the SEIA Regulations establishes that the environmental impact assessment
“(…) will consist of determining whether the predicted impacts constitute impacts
significant based on the criteria of article 11 of the Law, and detailed in Title II of this
Regulation.” In the case of environmental impacts, these “will be significant when they generate or
present any of the effects, characteristics or circumstances of article 11 of the Law, in accordance
to what is established in Title II of this regulation.”
To carry out the environmental evaluation, the following activities are considered:
- The valuation of environmental impacts
- The qualification of environmental impacts
5 The environmental components likely to be affected have been previously identified in the area chapter
of influence. In addition to the justification of why a given environmental component is or is not susceptible to being
affected.

4.3.1 Assessment and qualification of environmental impacts
The evaluation of each environmental impact on an element of the environment or attribute of the area
of influence is carried out through the product between environmental relevance and the importance of
impact, the result of which is the value of the environmental impact.
Equation 4-1. Environmental impact value
VIA= Ra x I
Where:
VIA: Environmental Impact Value
Ra: Environmental relevance
I: Importance of Impact
The proposed methodology weights the assessment of the importance of the impact by the relevance or
environmental valuation of each element or attribute of the area of influence in net terms and not
relative, since the objective of the impact evaluation considered by the SEIA regulations
It is not about identifying which element or attribute is more relevant than another, but rather what impacts are
significant and which are not.
Therefore, by not relativizing between factors, we avoid underestimating an impact for the sole fact that
an element or attribute is of little relevance compared to another in a certain area of
influence.
Having specified the above, the impacts will be classified according to the following scale:
Table 4-5. Classification of environmental impact values (VIA)
Environmental Impact Value Impact Rating
0 to -46 Not Significant
-47 to -93 Significant
Source: GAC
The classification presented establishes the difference between the impacts
not significant and those that
Yes, they are significant, in accordance with what is mentioned in the SEIA Regulations (D.S. N°40/2012),
considering a cut-off threshold equivalent to 50% of the scale.
Those environmental impacts that are classified as significant will also give rise to the
need to prepare the EIA, in accordance with the provisions of Article 11 of Law No. 19,300
4-24

EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
and, consequently, require that Mitigation, Repair and/or measures be proposed.
Compensation.
4.3.1.1 Determination of the relevance or environmental value of each component
The environmental relevance (Ra) of each environmental element or component that will be affected by
The Project is established based on a series of characteristics studied on the occasion of the
survey of the Project baseline that determines its quality or condition of importance
and uniqueness, at the discretion of the specialist, analyzing the relationship with other elements or attributes of the
area of influence; representativeness at the local and regional level; the abundance and state of
conservation, among others.
An ordinal scale is used with values ​​that vary between “Low” and “Extreme” relevance. This
scale is indicated in Table 4-6.
Table 4-6. Relevance rating scale.

The attributes used for the environmental assessment (Conesa Fernández, 2010)6 are the following:
• Abundance (Ab): If the environmental factor is found in large quantities in the environment, its
val
or decreases. If it is scarce, its value increases.
• Rarity (Ra): If the presence of the environmental factor in the area is something out of the ordinary, or a
particularity of the sector, something that does not commonly occur in the environment, its value increases.
If it has repetitive characteristics, or it is common to find the component in the sector, its
low value.
• Fragility (Fr): If the environmental factor is considered vulnerable, sensitive or weak, its value
go up. If it has resilience or is adaptable to changes, its value decreases.
• Diversity (Di): If the elements that make up the environmental factor are heterogeneous
(such as, for example: different textures, colors, shapes, species), its value increases. Yes
These elements are homogeneous, their value is reduced.
• Significance (Sig): If the environmental factor is considered to be of significance or
importance, whether due to social, historical, cultural, economic, ecological and/or
ecosystems, their value is high. If not, it's low.
• Historical-cultural Interest (IHC): The value of the environmental factor increases according to its peculiarity
historical, monumental and/or cultural.
• Difficulty of conservation (Dc): The assessment or relevance will be greater when the factor in
its current state, presents difficulties for its conservation.
Although the parameter relevance or environmental value is a function of the previous attributes that each
component uses, and, by the way, from the judgment of the specialist's technical criteria, the result should not
understood as the product of a mathematical equation, but as the result of the analysis on
the striking characteristics of each element or attribute of the area of influence. Thus, the relevance
environmental may be conditioned by one or more of the characteristics described. In this way,
avoid underestimating the relevance of the result of an average or other mathematical function
between the attributes. Therefore, the environmental relevance will be given by the following function of
description options:

RA= f (Ab, Ra, Fr, Di, Sig, IHC, Dc)
Additionally, the parameters included in the definition of the environmental relevance of each
component must consider climate change criteria in their assessment. The trends
projected in climate variables under a climate change scenario RCP 8.5 (scenario
severe) may generate changes in the assessment of the previous parameters.
As an example of the above, for the hydrology component the
assessment of the parameters rarity, fragility and significance in areas with trends of
decrease in precipitation or with greater risk of hydrological drought. On the other hand, the
flora and fauna components may see the value of the diversity parameter increased in areas
where there are increases in the risk of loss of diversity of flora or fauna species due to
changes in precipitation and temperature patterns.
The assessment of the parameters of environmental relevance, according to climate change criteria, must
be carried out for those components in which there are well-founded antecedents about their
susceptibility to the effects of climate change, and consequently there may be synergies
negative effects between the effects of the Project and climate change on the component.
For components in which there is a susceptibility to climate change or negative synergies,
Considering the analysis presented in Chapters 2 and 3 of this EIA, the assessment of the
environmental relevance will be carried out considering the possible evolution of the component under the
climate change scenario in its most unfavorable condition. In cases where there is no
susceptibility of the component to climate change or there are no negative synergies, the assessment
The relevance will be determined according to the current condition of the component. If the environmental relevance of
any component reaches the maximum rating in its current condition, it will not be considered an effect
addition of climate change on the valuation of the component
tea.

Expert judgment is essential in your selection. This is why, for each component
environmental, the criteria used for its assessment must be chosen and justified.
Expert judgment, according to the literature, is defined as: “an informed opinion of
people with experience in the subject, who are recognized by others as qualified experts in
this, and that can provide information, evidence, judgments and evaluations” (Escobar and Cuervo, 20087). In

4.3.1.2 Determination of the Importance of Environmental Impact
The importance of the impact (I) is determined based on a set of criteria descriptors of
according to the numerical methodology proposed by Conesa Fernández8, adapted by GAC as
as shown in the following equation:
Equation 4-2. Importance of the impact
I= Ca x (3Mag+2Ex+2Du+Re+SiCC+Si/AcOp+Pr)
9
Where:
Ca: Character or nature of the impact
Mag: Magnitude
Ex: Extension
Du: Duration
Re: Reversibility
SiCC: Climate Change Synergy
Yes/AcOp: Synergy/Accumulation with other projects
Pr: Periodicity
The adaptation proposed by GAC in relation to the indicated bibliographic reference is related
with:
• Dispense with the criterion called “Moment” since it implies underestimating
the magnitude of impacts that will not occur immediately but years after the
action that generates it. In this case, the environmental legislation in force in the country does not consider
such possibility of mitigating the magnitude of environmental impacts.
8 Source: Consesa Fernández, V. (2010). Methodological guide for environmental impact assessment. World Editions
Press, Madrid. Page 235.

Rare Earth Concentrate
• Dispense with the criterion called “Effect” since it could lead to
underestimate the magnitude of indirect impacts, attenuation that does not consider the
current environmental legislation in the country.
• Incorporate a divider (9) whose sole purpose is to allow working with a numerical scale
easier to handle, without affecting the final impact rating.

duration of environmental impacts with respect to the given criteria that gives you

4.3.2 Justification of the impact assessment methodology
Article 18, letter f), of the RSEIA, states the following:
“The prediction of environmental impacts will be made based on models, simulations,
measurements or mathematical calculations. When, due to its nature, an impact cannot be
quantify, your prediction will only have a qualitative character.
The use of procedures or methodologies necessary to meet the requirement indicated in the
previous paragraph must be duly justified.”
From the above it is understood that in the event that the impacts cannot be quantified through
of models, measurements or mathematical calculations, the impacts must be evaluated in a way
qualitative. That is why certain impacts are evaluated qualitatively.
In order to identify an appropriate qualitative methodology to determine whether the works and/or
Project activities will generate significant impacts on some element of the environment
The literature associated with impact evaluation was reviewed. As a result of the bibliographic review
It was decided to use the impact evaluation proposal developed by V. Conesa Fernández
(1997)14, since it describes the criteria that could be used to identify and evaluate
qualitatively the impacts of the projects. Based on these criteria, the most
appropriate, considering that: “the value of a factor or an inventory unit is directly
proportional to the degree of qualitative characterization” (Conesa Fernández, 1997, Page 85).
As Conesa Fernández (1997, Page 22) points out, the objective of the evaluation is to facilitate the
development of projects, ensuring sustainable management of resources:
“These evaluations aim, as a principle, to establish a balance between the development of
human activity and the Environment, without trying to become a negative and
obstructionist, nor a brake on development, but rather an operational instrument to prevent
overexploitation of the natural environment and a brake on negative and anarchic development. Each
project, work or activity will cause a disturbance to the environment in which it is located, the
14 Source: Conesa Fernández, V. (1997). Methodological guide for environmental impact assessment. World Editions
Press, Madrid. Page 85.

==================================================================================

==============

Rare Earth Concentrate
which must be minimized based on the environmental impact studies that due to the
"Their execution will be carried out by the relevant technicians."
In accordance with the above, the qualitative methodology used in this EIA has been
developed by those who subscribe using Conesa's proposal as a theoretical basis
Fernández (1997)15, and the experience of his multidisciplinary team. This theoretical base has been
used in the majority of the Environmental Impact Studies that have entered the System of
Environmental Impact Assessment, since the General Environmental Bases Law was published
(No. 19,300).

environmental of the Project.
4.3.3 Impact Evaluation Results
This section develops the evaluation of impacts by component likely to be affected.
4.3.3.1 Air quality
i. Environmental relevance of air quality
Within the framework of the development of the Project, most of the activities involve a
generation of atmospheric emissions, both particulate matter in its different fractions
(MP, MP and MP30), such as internal combustion product gases (CO, HC/VOC, NOx, NH and
10 2.5 3
SOx) from machinery and vehicle engines.
During the construction, operation and closure phase of the Project, the activities generating
particulate matter are mainly related to excavation, filling, turning of material and
resuspension of dust due to vehicle traffic on unpaved roads. On the other hand, the
Combustion gas generating activities are associated with emissions from the combustion of
engines, both machinery and transport vehicles.

lower emissions. Emissions in detail by type of source, phase and year of the Project are
presented in Annex 1-3 “Estimation of Atmospheric Emissions” of the EIA.

The current situation in which the Project is located is included in the dispersion analysis of

To evaluate the impact of the Project, with respect to the characterized baseline situation, it is
evaluates the contribution in terms of concentration of contaminants, in the recorded measurements
by the monitoring station and in the identified receptors of interest.
The assessment of the relevance of “Air Quality” is considered Extreme (10) by virtue of the
significance of the element object of protection since, regardless of its current state, the quality
of air corresponds to an element that is regulated in order to protect both the
health of the population, as well as biodiversity.
ii. Identified impacts
a) ICA-01: Affectation of human receptors due to increased concentration of
particulate matter and gases
Construction phase
During the construction phase of the Project, it will last 25 months, the
authorization of the exploitation areas (ZE), disposal area (ZD) Jupiter and the storage area
vegetables (ZAV). Specifically, activities are contemplated for escarpment and extraction of waste from ZE and
earth moving work and land preparation for the location area of the
Processing Plant and temporary storage areas for plant material. Likewise, all these
Activities involve the activity of machinery and transport vehicles. Emission sources
with the associated activities are presented in Table 4-14.

Operation Phase
The operation phase has a total duration of 6 years, however, year number 4 of said phase
corresponds to the most conservative analysis scenario, since the highest rate of
atmospheric emissions, therefore, it is used this year as a representation of the 6-year scenario
duration of the operation phase.
During the course of year 4 of operation, which, as mentioned above, corresponds
to the scenario with higher emissions, it is projected
the operation of the Victoria North ZE and ZE
Maite for the extraction of material, and the Neptuno ZD for the disposal of sterile and maicillo
washed and exhausted granite. The emission sources are presented in Table 4-15 below.
identified for year 4 of the operation phase along with the revenue-generating activities
emissions, related to each source.

Below are the results of the modeling according to atmospheric pollutant.
evaluated for this phase. Tables are presented where the contribution of each pollutant is quantified.
evaluated of the Project, for all the defined recipients, which correspond to nearby homes
to the Kingston College Air Quality Monitoring Station and Project.
It should be reiterated that the results presented below are calculated based on the emissions
atmospheric emissions generated in year 4 of operation, corresponds to the most conservative scenario of
analysis, since the highest rate of atmospheric emissions will be generated, therefore, it is used this year
as a conservative representative of the scenario of the 6 years that the operation phase lasts. In the
Annex 4-1 atmospheric emissions modeling, the methodology and results are presented in detail
obtained with respect to the estimated contributions to air quality for the execution of the Project.
The evaluation considers a total of 21 receivers, 1 of them correspond to the quality station
from the air Kingston College and 20 to discrete receivers of interest, mostly homes. For the
air quality station and discrete receivers of interest, the air quality line is presented
projected (CAP), which considers the sum of the measured baseline (LoB), the contributions of other
projects with favorable RCA that have not been executed (OP), and the Project contribution (AP). For
evaluate the contributions of the Project in the discrete receivers, other than the monitoring station of
air quality, the levels measured at the Kington College station are considered as the baseline,
because it corresponds to the closest EMRP monitoring station, and is in a sector without
presence of industrial activities, as occurs with defined discrete receptors.

In accordance with the general criteria provided by the SEA, prior to carrying out the evaluation of the
population health risk, it is necessary to determine the scenario in which the
Project, confirming whether the nearby population could be affected by the effects, characteristics or
circumstances referred to in letter a) of article 11 of Law No. 19,300. This analysis results from
great relevance because formally the commune of Penco is included in the “Plan de
Prevention and Atmospheric Decontamination for the Communes of Concepción Metropolitano”
(DS Nº6/2018 of the MMA); This, as a consequence of its inclusion within, the declaration as
“Saturated Zone for Respirable Fine Particulate Material (PM2.5)” (DS Nº15/2015 of the MMA),
as daily concentration.
From the review of the behavior of the air quality monitoring stations of
population representativeness (EMRP) that have been included in the definition of “saturated zone”, it is
possible to infer that the saturation condition occurs heterogeneously in the area where
The prevention and decontamination plan is applied. Kingston College station, which is the most
close to the Project, and is located in a sector without the presence of industrial activities, being
therefore representative of the exposure situation of discrete human receptors
defined as relevant to this project, the measurements of recent years (2020-2022)
show that the limits of the primary quality standard for MP2.5 are not exceeded on average
triannual of recent years and not in the 98th percentile of 24 hours 2022, only reaching
69% for the three-year average and 75% for the daily norm. Consequently, in terms

In this way, the effects on the health of the human population due to exposure to
MP2.5 for each human receptor in the area of influence of the Project, for year 4 of the

From the bibliographic review carried out to the set of methodologies used to evaluate effects on
health due to particulate matter, the WHO in its HRAPIE18 report and its recent update of
The global air quality guidelines19 recommend evaluating the health risk for the purposes
acute (cardiovascular and respiratory hospitalizations) and chronic (where the best effect is
account of health risk is general mortality less external causes), since in these
categories is where there is sufficient scientific evidence.
From the review of alternatives
To characterize the concentration-response relationship, in general
can conclude that the methodologies have been very consistent in the studies carried out both
international level like those carried out in Chile. For this analysis, the model was used
recommended by the WHO20, which collects the accumulated experience of the EPA and others
researchers, from which the short- and long-term exposure model is applied to the material
particulate matter and its health effects. It should be noted that this model was also used by Luis
Cifuentes21 for the study carried out on the definition of the PM2.5 standard aimed at identifying and
quantify the health impacts derived from emissions of pollutants into the air, which
reinforces that this analysis methodology is totally valid for this case.
When assessing risk from exposure, regulatory agencies, such as Health Canada and the
Environmental Protection Agency of the United States (U.S. EPA), it is recognized that any level of
Non-zero exposure is associated with some cancer risk. Therefore, these agencies
International organizations have defined the level of risk that could be considered acceptable or tolerable. At
In this regard, all agencies agree that a risk level of 10-6 attributable to a project
can be considered as “essentially zero” or acceptable risk level. However,
The agencies also agree that between an absolute health risk of the order of 10-4 to 10-6
could be considered an “acceptable health risk depending on the situation and circumstances.”
of exposure.”

present in leaves can be washed away by rain, mostly coarse particulate material.

iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) ICA-01 Affectation of human receptors due to increased concentration of
particulate matter and gases
Construction Phase
The emissions generated by the project in the construction phase suggest a negative character
(Ca=-1) due to the contribution that the Project will generate on the baseline situation. Its magnitude will imply
changes in the baseline (Mag=2), however, the greatest contributions are expected in recipients
isolated areas close to the project (approximately 150 m). The estimated emissions for the
construction are of a smaller magnitude than those estimated for the operation phase, therefore, the
Expected contributions in terms of air quality will be smaller. The execution of
Project will not generate an exceedance of the primary air quality regulations in any of the

evaluated recipients. The extent of the impact will be maximum or total (Ex=8), since the impact will be
will manifest throughout the entire area of influence. The duration of the impact is temporary (Du=2) since
which is limited to the construction phase that will last 2 years. It is totally reversible (Re=1), since,
Once the project is completed, emissions will not be generated. The synergy with climate change is
evaluates as simple (SiCC=1), since during the construction phase it is not expected to be
register changes, as a result of climate change, that modify the estimated emissions and contributions.
This is a synergistic/cumulative impact (Si/AcOp=4), because the magnitude, duration and
extension of the effect of other projects can modify the effect of the Project alone.
Corresponds to a continuous impact (Pr=4), since the activities generate emissions
continuously.
With the above, the importance of the impact rises to -4.0. It is important to indicate that the
PM10 emissions will be offset by 120% for the construction phase of the Project.

smaller magnitude than those estimated for the operation phase, therefore, the expected contributions in
terms of air quality will be of lesser magnitude. The execution of the Project will not generate a
exceedance of the secondary reference standards in none of the evaluated receivers. The
extension of the impact will be maximum (Ex=8), since the impact will manifest itself in the entire area
of influence. The duration of the impact is temporary (Du=2) since it is limited to the construction phase
which will last 2 years. It is completely reversible (Re=1), since, once the project is finished, it is not
will generate emissions. The synergy with climate change is evaluated as simple (SiCC=1), since
that during the construction phase no changes are expected to be recorded as a result of the change
climate change, which modifies the estimated emissions and contributions. It is an impact
synergistic/cumulative (Si/AcOp=4), because magnitude, duration and extension of the effect of others
Projects can modify the effect of the Project on its own. Corresponds to a continuous impact
(Pr=4), since the activities continuously generate emissions.
With the above, the importance of the impact rises to -4.0.

As can be seen from the modeling for the construction and operation phases of the Project, the
larger areas where exceedances of recommended thresholds could occur
They correspond to the Amphibious Class, extending outside the Project intervention areas. In
However, for reptiles, mammals and birds, the distances are smaller, limited to the areas themselves.
of intervention.
In this sense, and as established in the technical document “Evaluation criteria in the SEIA:
Evaluation of impacts due to noise on native fauna” when the receptors present a level of
exposure to noise that exceeds the reference thresholds associated with behavioral effects, must
evaluate the significance of the impact on the species evaluated with respect to:
- Affectation of the permanence of the resource, in this case, native fauna.
- Alteration of the regeneration or renewal capacity of the resource.
- Alteration of the conditions that make possible the presence and development of species and
ecosystems, with special emphasis on those resources of the country that are scarce,
unique and representative.
In this case, and for the Amphibian Class, given that they are rare, sensitive and
low mobility, it is estimated that exposure to noise levels above reference thresholds
can alter the conditions that make the presence and development of species possible. For what
Therefore, the level of environmental relevance for this factor will be considered extreme (10) for
wildlife receptors associated with the Amphibian Class For the other groups (reptiles, mammals and
birds) a moderate environmental relevance is defined (4).
The environmental relevance of the noise component reached its maximum value in its current condition,
without considering climate change scenarios.

iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) RU-01: Risk to the health of the population due to increased levels of
sound pressure
Construction Phase
This impact has been rated as negative (Ca=-1) in all sectors, due to the fact that the
Project will generate an increase in noise over the basal condition (background noise), which will be
exercised by the use of various heavy machinery for construction activities. The
magnitude is medium (Mag=2) because the degree of alteration implies changes with respect to the
basal condition, but within acceptable ranges. For its part, the Extension is considered as
wide (Ex=3), since the noise levels will manifest outside the immediate surroundings of the
source or in different sectors of AI. The Duration (Du=2) is considered temporary or transitory
because the construction of the project (2 years) will generate an increase in noise levels

ace Rare
only during the construction period, in the same way Reversibility will be short term
(Re=1), since it is considered that at this stage the impact is not reversed in a period of less than 1
year. No changes are projected due to climate change (SiCC=0), and Synergy/Accumulation with
other projects (Si/AcOp=1) resulted in slightly Synergistic. With respect to Periodicity, the
effect is classified as Continuous (Pr=4). According to the above, the importance of this impact
is -2.2.

This impact has been rated as negative (Ca=-1) in all sectors, due to the fact that the

4.3.3.3 Vibrations
i. Environmental relevance Vibrations
The assessment of the relevance of the “Vibration Levels” was established as extreme (10),
considering that vibration levels are established by parameters or thresholds
international reference, corresponding to the American standard of the U.S. Federal Transit
Administration (FTA) Report, “Transit Noise and Vibration Impact Assessment, which establishes
immission limits for different land uses or degrees of sensitivity, in order to verify their
compliance.

4.3.3.4 Geomorphology, geological and geomorphological risks
i. Environmental relevance Geomorphology, geological risks and
geomorphological
Depending on the characterization carried out in the Section
3.4, 3.5 and 3.6 of Chap. 3 Baseline
(Section A), it has been determined that the geomorphological composition of the area in which
The location of the Project is disruptive in nature. The relief is complex with varied slopes, which
They range from flat areas to areas of abrupt changes. Figure 4-13 shows the gradient
of the slope, with which it can be seen that near the coast, a steeper slope dominates.
constant, while the changes in slopes become sharp when moving towards the
west, in the Coastal Mountain Range. In the Coastal Mountain Range, within the area of influence of the
Project, modeling by Slope ranges (Figure 4-13), shows that the relief is complex,
with varied slopes.
4-93
==================================================================================
PAGE 103
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Figure 4-13. Slope gradient and slope model for component influence area
Geomorphology
Source: GAC, Chapter 3
According to Börgel (1983), this area is called Central Lacustrine and the Glacio-Fluvio-Volcanic Plain,
where there is a decrease in the height of the Andes Mountains, the central plain,
Coastal mountain range and coastal areas. There are also lake basins, due to the
tectonic and glacial action. Specifically, the Project is located in the geomorphological unit
corresponding to the western flank of the Coastal Mountain Range. The latter is presented in a way
convex, with altitudes no greater than 300 meters above sea level, with slopes that generally fluctuate
from low (0 – 2°) to very steep (>35°) and to moderately steep (20° – 30°). The slopes
may present an advanced degree of physical and chemical weathering evidenced by the presence
of regolith, which shows the decomposition of rocks.
Now, given the geomorphological characteristics of the area in which the Project is located, as well
as well as other variables such as presence or absence of vegetation, the main risk
identified corresponds to those of mass removal. They were identified in the Project area,
deposits of mass removals located and limited to areas with an absence of vegetation and/or
where a highly weathered slope or slope is exposed, which favors landslides and
removal of the surface layer; These localized mass movements are associated with slopes
4-94
==================================================================================
PAGE 104
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
anthropic lands and areas of anthropic terraces present in the place. The risk of removal in
mass is associated with a process of slow or rapid mobilization of a certain volume of soil,
rock or both, in various proportions, and generated by various factors (Hauser, 1993). These
Movements have a descending character since they are fundamentally controlled by the
severity (Cruden, 1991).
The triggering factors of a removal process are related to the susceptibility that
presents a slope, depending on different interactions, either in the interaction of agents
conditioning factors such as: geology, geotechnics, geomorphology, hydrology and hydrogeology, vegetation,
climate and anthropogenic activity; and/or depending on triggering agents such as
precipitation, earthquakes and other less frequent factors such as volcanic activity,
snow melting, anthropogenic factors, etc. (Lara et al, 2008).
The methodology used to define the potential is a susceptibility analysis, based on the
works by Mora (2004) who defines “that it must be considered that landslides occur
when on a slope, composed of a specific lithology, with a certain degree of slope,
reaches a degree of susceptibility (passive elements). Under these conditions, the factors
external and dynamic elements (active elements), such as seismicity and rainfall, act as factors
“triggers that disturb the balance that is maintained on the slope.”
This is how it is considered that
The degree of susceptibility to slip is the product of the passive elements and the action
of the triggering factors:
H = EP x G
Where H is the degree of susceptibility to slip, EP is the value product of the combination
of the passive elements, and G the value of the triggering factors or active elements.
For its part, the value of the passive elements is made up of the following parameters:
EP = SI x Sh x Sp
Where SI is the value of the lithological susceptibility parameter, Sh is the value of the
susceptibility due to soil moisture, and Sp the value of the susceptibility parameter due to
pending.
The value of active elements is made up of the following parameters:
G = Ds + Dll
4-95
==================================================================================
PAGE 105
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Where Ds is the value of the seismic tripping parameter and Dll is the value of the tripping parameter.
due to rain
The analysis of each of the parameters detailed above (further references in
Chapter 3-A, Baseline, Physical Environment, Section 3.6.4) according to the algebraic expression
raised in the methodology, delivery for the area of influence, the distribution of susceptibility
of mass removal processes (Figure 4-14).
Figure 4-14 Susceptibility of mass removal, for the Area of Influence
Source: GAC, Chapter 3
The result shows that the maximum value obtained is 216, a value that is considered under all circumstances.
time that the maximum considered permissible by the methodology is 1,800; that is,
percentage wise, the worst theoretically possible scenario for the Project's AI represents
percentage wise only 12% of the worst case tolerated by the method.
As indicated, the Project location corresponds to an area of heterogeneous topography,
which presents various ranges of slopes. In the defined area of influence, the slope factor
It is the one with the greatest weight when estimating susceptibility to mass removal processes. Of
this way, given the homogeneous conditions for the other factors that are included in the

Rare Earth Concentrate
calculation, in the sectors with lower slopes, the risks of occurrence of mass removals
are low, while the sectors with greater slopes present greater susceptibility. In
The area of influence of this component dominates a moderate risk, however, they are not
absent the sectors with high susceptibility, which must be evaluated and identified
previously in order to carry out the measures that are necessary for prevention.
Based on the background presented above and the impact considered for these
components “Increased risk of mass removal due to alteration of geoforms”, the
Environmental Relevance is considered Moderate (6), since, although sectors with
greater susceptibility given its conditions, the worst scenario theoretically possible

method.
ii. Identified Impacts
a) IGE-01: Increased risk of mass removal due to alteration of geoforms
Construction Phase
The Project during its construction phase involves an alteration of local geoforms,
mainly through the preparation of the land for the activities to be carried out during
the next phase of operation.
Operation Phase
Specifically, within the ZE and ZD there are some sectors of hillsides with slopes.
pronounced, and therefore susceptible to mass removal events, however, the
Project engineering considers measures to avoid this situation, specifically communication channels.
contour of these areas, with the precise purpose of channeling rainwater, preventing it from
come into contact with the interior of them, thus avoiding the generation
mass removal.
Closing Phase
During the closure phase, no impacts on Geomorphology and Geological Risks are expected -
Geomorphological, since no additional parts, works and actions will be carried out to those declared
for the construction or operation phase of the Project.

iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) IGE-01: Increased risk of mass removal due to alteration of geoforms
Construction Phase
The impact has been classified as negative (Ca=-1), since it implies a deterioration and modification
in the basal condition of the existing geomorphology, increasing the risk of mass removal.
Of High Magnitude (Mag=4), since the construction of the Project's superficial works will generate
a modification to the existing relief that implies considerable changes with respect to the condition
basal. Of broad extension (Ex=3), since the impact manifests itself outside the immediate environment of
the source, in this case, of the activity generating the alterations to the geoforms and condition
basal. Its Duration (Du=2), since the manifestation and permanence is constant. of character
irreversible (Re=4) since the installation of the works does not allow reversibility until these
activities that will cause alteration to the geoforms are dismantled and ceased. The impact
manifests itself with a simple synergism (SiCC=1), since the risk due to climate change
associated with the component under evaluation is low. It has a slight accumulation (Si/AcOp=1), since the
magnitude, duration and joint extent do not modify the effect of the project alone. The
periodicity is continuous (Pr=4), since the effect on the area where the works are located
permanent ones manifest themselves with a continuous periodicity.

4.3.3.5 Hydrology
i. Hydrology environmental relevance
In general terms, the environmental component of hydrology is relevant in the management
sustainable management of water resources, the protection of aquatic ecosystems and the prevention of
water-related natural disasters, as well as for understanding climate change and
its effects on the availability and quality of water.
4-99
==================================================================================
PAGE 109
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
For the particular case, the area of hydrological influence of the Project is located in one of the
coastal subbasins of the Penco estuaries and the Andalién River in the Biobío region, Commune of Penco,
whose hydrological regime corresponds to basins with a strict pluvial feeding regime, for
which the distribution of flows during the year is conditioned to the occurrence of
precipitation and its balance conditioned by system losses: Evapotranspiration and
resource extraction (surface and underground).
In accordance with what is described in chapter 1 of this EIA, the activity derived from the exploitation
of rare earths would generate the temporary modification of the drainage pattern within said basin,
as a consequence of the construction and maintenance of a series of civil works on
intermittent runoff streams of the caisson and culvert type that would allow traffic
of vehicles and machinery during all phases of the project.
As analyzed in the hydrology baseline, this component is susceptible to being affected
by climate change, mainly through the variability of certain parameters that
influence their availability. Indeed, the simulation (Average value) derived from the data of
ArClimb (MMA) predicts an increase in maximum temperatures for the commune (and the sub-basin)
daily average of 1°C by the year 2060, and along with it the increase in the probability of
drought and dry days; and consequently an acceleration in the evapotranspiration rate
product of climate changes. In the case of maximum daily rainfall, this is
projected below historical maximums, which corresponds to a condition that would affect
the inputs to the basin's water system; However, the projection of the intensity of
Precipitation forecasts an increase in frequency of 10% at intensities of 2 mm/day.
Given the interaction of this set of variables, it is expected that the water resource presents
conditions that reduce its availability in the Project area, although these
decreases in frequency or quantity respond to slight margins, without modifying the trends
described for the area.
Based on this background, the assessment of the environmental relevance of the hydrology component
should be maintained or increased slightly due to lower future availability in the
Project environment.
Taking into consideration the above, its high vulnerability, with a value
high socioeconomic level, and the fact that water quality requirements are regulated by the
current national regulations NCh 1333:1978 Mod. 1987 of the MOP and international parameters of
reference, the level of environmental relevance for this factor will be considered high (9).

Rare Earth Concentrate

Operation Phase
According to the hydrology of the project site basin, the feeding of the
streams comes from a strict rainfall regime, with dendritic drainage that could be
interrupted by the actions of the project in its operation, such as maintenance
scheduled of its hydraulic works.
In accordance with section 1.9.8.3 of the project description, for each extraction zone (ZE),
disposal area (ZD) and topsoil collection area (ZAV) hydraulic works will be enabled
in order to capture the runoff generated and return it to the basins and/or streams most
nearby, these works will correspond to evacuation and contour channels, discharge works,
junctions and small depressions in the ground, in which pumping is contemplated
to restore water resources to the transport channels (contour).
The conceptual aspects associated with the restrictions generated by the operation in the areas of
extraction, which were considered for the design of the drainage system are described in the
following points:
• The design of the drainage system must consider that its hydraulic conduction capacity
allow at most to stop activities due to rain for a maximum of 10 days a year.
For this purpose, the storm that is exceeded 10 days a year and with a probability
occurrence of 5% of the years.
• The geometry of the channeling for the collection and conduction of rainwater from each
platform, must be restricted to a maximum width inside the platforms of at most
1 meter, while it is considered that it does not generate interference with the traffic of the
vehicles during the extraction operation.
4-107
==================================================================================
PAGE 117
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
• The definition of the drainage network, fundamentally composed of a berm at the foot of the
slope, you must take into account that the development of the excavations is carried out in two phases
construction projects temporarily out of date, ensuring the coordination of the drainage network
between both phases.
• The drainage network inside the extraction area must consider discharging the water
towards contour channels, which in turn will lead the waters to the natural channels
receptors of surface runoff.
• The drainage channels will be located at the junction vertex formed by the meeting
between the excavation slope and the excavation platform.
• Gravitational runoff in the drainage network is fundamentally considered,
the runoff characteristics being conditioned by the geometry of the section
transversal of the runoff section and fundamentally by the slope
longitudinally, the platforms will be developed with a minimum transverse slope towards
the driving gutter, in order to facilitate the drainage of rainwater.

Construction Phase
The parts and works of the project that are related to possible interactions with bodies of
surface water are the construction of accesses and internal roads; and the authorization of the
extraction zones (ZE), disposal (ZD) and storage (ZAV). These are described in the
identification and sources of impact of the IOH-01-Co impact from the previous section.
To carry out the construction works of the project, the intervention of channels is required
natural areas in order to implement access works and internal roads, in addition to the authorization
of the extraction zones (3), Disposal Zone (1) and a Vegetable Storage Zone (ZAV), as well as
also the modification of a section of the ENAP pipeline, making it necessary to intervene
26 crossings.
It should be noted that, as indicated above, the different streams or channels
Natural areas have a rainfall regime, and therefore their greatest contribution in flows is
conditioned to the presence of precipitation, which for the project area develops
during the winter season.
4-108
==================================================================================
PAGE 118
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
It is important to consider that the works to intervene in natural channels have measures
operational measures aimed at minimizing the effects on water quality during the
construction and operation of the project, which have been described in detail in Annex 10-
12 PAS 156. In summary, the measures are the following:
• Training of Workers regarding the importance of water resources and the
pollutants.
• The personnel in charge of the works will be trained with the objective of preserving the conditions of
streams and avoid disturbance by elements, materials or substances other than those
of the ravines. A record of this activity will be maintained at the work facility.
• Handling of contaminating elements or materials in the installation of tasks on site
determined for this.
• It will be prohibited to carry out any type of repair or maintenance of vehicles or machinery.
in the work fronts and sites surrounding the channels.
On the other hand, the Project will use vehicles in good condition and with up-to-date technical inspections,
considering carrying out maintenance, thus avoiding any accidental spillage of
fuel or hydrocarbons in streams.
It should also be noted that the Project will manage its waste in accordance with current regulations.
enabling temporary collection places for the storage of waste, either in the
installation of tasks during the construction phase, in the processing plant sector and
in all sectors enabled for such purposes.
This whole set of measures will allow us to avoid any type of alteration in the quality of the
surface waters during the construction phase.

4.3.3.6 Soil
i. Soil environmental relevance
The environmental relevance of the soil component is established based on the Capacity Class of
Use, determined at the baseline according to the criteria of the Soil Study Guideline
of the SAG 2011 (rectified)23, its ability to establish species or biodiversity and the availability of the
resource at the regional and community level.
The Land Use Capacity (CCUS), in its broadest concept, represents the ability of the
soils to execute functions (intrinsic or extrinsic) in the magnitude that are inherent to them, which
derives from the set of physical, chemical and biological properties that they possess and that allows them
function as a living open system within the limits of the ecosystem to which they belong,
of the given use, sustain biological production and the life of the organisms that are sustained by it.
The grouping of soils in CCUS is an order that allows us to indicate their adaptability to certain
crops and indicates difficulties and risks that may arise when using them. The Guidelines to Apply to
Feasibility Report Requests for Non-Agricultural Constructions in Rural Areas
23 Source: SAG. (2011, rectified 2016). Guidelines for soil study. Santiago, Chile. MINAGRI. 26 pp.
4-113
==================================================================================
PAGE 123
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
(IFC) of SAG (2019)24, considers soils of high agricultural priority to be those classified in the classes
of usability I, II and III. The priority of soils is based on the best properties and aptitudes
for food production and the development of ecological functions of soils, in and of themselves,
scarce.
According to the profiles described in the field, it was observed that, in general, they correspond to soils
deep, greater than 90 cm deep, with a structure of medium subangular blocks
moderate, which can be observed up to 90 cm deep or be massive (without structure)
from 70 cm; The textures in the profile range from loamy to clayey, it being common to observe texture
clay loam; a low presence or absence of surface stoniness, and a low presence or absence
absence of stoniness in the soil profile; Furthermore, they correspond to non-saline soils, not
sodic and non-calcareous. For its part, the limiting feature of these soils corresponds to
to the slope, due to the position of hills with slopes of different inclinations, identifying a
tendency towards steeply undulating slopes
ladas (15 to <30%) and hills (30 to <45%). Of this
way, according to what was observed on the ground, the soils described in the project area
They correspond to soils of Class IVs2, VIs2, VIIs2 and VIIIs2 of Usability. in a small
proportion (0.48 ha), the limitation is due to usable water, classifying it in VIs8. How to

priority for agricultural lands.
According to the background reviewed above, it is possible to point out that, although they are soils
of moderate agricultural priority, they are deep with little or no stoniness, good or very good
moisture retention capacity (usable water), which are favorable parameters in
determine the quality of the soil, its only limitation being the slope. Added to the above, your
Representativeness in the commune is very low. Considering the above, it is justified to grant a
high relevance.

The P95 percentile of the registry does not present a clear pattern of increase or decrease on an annual scale or
in the autumn, winter and spring seasons, although the increasing trend presents a
greater significance for the summer season. AND
Based on this background, and taking into account
Since the useful life of the Project is less than 20 years, a negative effect of the change is not projected
climate on the soil component. Since there is no clear pattern of increase or decrease in
maximum daily rainfall during high rainfall seasons, not possible
establish that climate change may increase the risk of soil erosion. They are discarded
negative synergies between the possible effects of the Project and climate change on this
component. The possible effects of the Project on the soil component will be evaluated
according to the current condition of this component, and not according to its possible evolution under
climate change scenarios.

ii. Identified Impacts
a) ISU-01: Loss of natural resource soil
The loss of a natural resource is the irreversible loss of a land surface generated
due to the location or permanent occupation in a rural area. The Project will generate loss
permanent land as a consequence of the construction and operation of its works. This impact
This is due to the fact that the Project works require soil intervention for their authorization.
Initially, through the escarpment prior to the authorization of the works, however, the
impact as loss of soil, due to the characteristics of the works with greater occupation of
surface, corresponding to the Extraction Zones (ZE) and Disposal Zone (ZD).
In each ZE (Victoria Norte, Luna and Maite), after the escarpment, material will continue to be extracted,
carrying out excavations at greater depth, corresponding to the waste that will be taken to the ZD
(Neptune) for disposal during the construction phase, as well as the mineral that will be
transferred to the Plant for processing in the operation phase. That is, on the surface of
each ZE, the soil will be lost, according to the progress of the works. For its part, on the surface of the ZD
Neptune, after making the escarpment, will dispose of both the waste coming from the ZE
in the construction and operation phases, such as the mineral already processed in the Plant
Processing during the operation phase, that is, the soil will be lost, according to the progress of
the
works.
Likewise, the loss of soil on the surface on which the Plant will be located is considered.
Processing, due to the movement of earth and scarp required to level the land. Also
there will be loss of soil due to the creation of the planned roads, considering the topography
undulating and hilly areas of the place, since it will be necessary to make cuts and fillings. It is not considered
loss of soil in the plant soil collection area.
The intervention surfaces in the construction and operation phases, the detail is presented in the
Table 4-87 and Table 4-88, respectively.

b) ISU-02: Loss of the capacity to sustain biodiversity due to erosion
The Project corresponds to the construction and operation of a mining site that will extract Lands
Rare. For the extractive process, specific exploitation areas designated as
Extraction Zones (ZE) Victoria Norte, Maite and Luna, from where the Rare Earths will be extracted.
On the other hand, waste collection will be carried out in the area designated as the Disposal Zone (ZD).
Neptune. Both the ZE and the ZD contemplate vegetation removal activities, movement
of land, and change in the general geoform of the area where they are located. Consequently, they can
also constitute changes in the erosive processes (mainly water erosion) present in
the area.
A water erosion risk map was prepared (See Annex 4-6 Erosion Risk Map), both
for the current situation as well as for a Project situation. Erosion Risk Maps
Current and Potential Erosion Risk were developed from the methodology established by
Castro (2016), for the entire Project Area of Influence.
Regarding the current risk of erosion, it is possible to point out that the majority of the soil (81%) has a
“low” risk with 191.77 ha, followed by “medium” risk with 18.40 ha (7.8%), in the condition without

project. 10.8% of the surfaces (25.29 ha) are classified as “other uses”, that is, sectors that
They have already been intervened and are not considered land.
On the other hand, the risk of potential erosion or “with project” presents an important variation
with respect to the current condition, since the actions and works of the project modify the indices of

iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) ISU-01: Loss of Natural Soil Resource
Construction Phase
This impact has been classified as Negative (Ca=-1), since it implies a loss of
resource. The magnitude of this impact is classified as maximum or total (Mag=12) since the ground
where the works will be built will be without the possibility of use because its impact is total. The
Extension of the impact is classified as punctual (Ex=1), because the impact only manifests
in the sectors where the works or actions are located (37.44 ha). It will have a permanent effect
or constant (Du=2) and irreversible (Re=4), because the natural restitution capacity
will occur within a period of more than 15 years. It is considered that there is no synergy with climate change
(SiCC=0) and it is slightly synergistic with other projects (Si/AcOP=1), since the surface area
of influence of the component interacts with the project “Operational Continuity Center of
Concepción Waste Management” with RCA. The Periodicity is continuous (Pr=4) since the
Manifestation of soil loss will occur throughout the construction period and will be
will maintain during the operation phase. According to the above, the importance of this impact
corresponds to -5.9.

4.3.3.7 Plants (flora and vegetation)
i. Environmental relevance plants (flora and vegetation)
The quantification and qualification of the environmental relevance of the Plants component (flora and
vegetation) was carried out based on the vegetation formations and terrestrial vascular flora defined
in the area of influence (AI) described in Chapter 03 “Baseline”, Section B, based on the
environmental uniqueness criteria listed in the CONAF Environmental Assessment Guide (2020).
The Project is located in the commune of Penco and Concepción, Province of Concepción, Region of
Biobío and considers an area of 673.62 ha. According to the classification of Gajardo (1994), the area of
Project is inserted within the Deciduous Forest Region, in the Forest subregion
Llano Deciduous Forest, specifically in the formation of the Concepción Deciduous Forest. This
formation extends along the low and middle slopes of the Coastal Mountain Range, in the Region of
Biobío, presenting a humid phase towards the oceanic slope and a dry phase towards the east.
Originally it must have had great floristic development and richness, and a
strong penetration of laurifolia species in the typical physiognomy of deciduous trees
dominant, in addition, being the geographical area of the oak (Nothofagus obliqua), but it has been almost
completely replaced by Pinus radiata plantations.
According to Luebert and Pliscoff (2019), the Project is located in two (2) formations. one
corresponding to the Sclerophyllous Forest, specifically to the vegetation floor Sclerophyllous Forest
coastal Mediterranean of Lithrea caustica - Azara integrifolia, and the other called formation of the
Deciduous forest, specifically the vegetation floor Mediterranean coastal deciduous forest
of Nothofagus obliqua - Gomortega keule.
4-123
==================================================================================
PAGE 133
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
Based on the results of the component baseline (Chapter 03, Section B), it was determined that
The intervened environments cover the largest surface of the area of influence, reaching 71% of
the total area (478.44 ha), followed by the natural environment with 121.02 ha (18%) and in third place
the modified environment with 74.16 ha (11%). In general, it can be indicated that AI is composed
mainly by forest plantations and some harvested sectors, followed by
forest formations, both native and wild, and shrublands with and without co-dominance of
tree species.
Regarding the vegetation formations in intervened environments, the Eucalyptus Plantation
globulus, Pinus radiata feral forest, Pinus radiata plantation and feral forest
of Eucalyptus globulus are the ones that predominate within the area of influence, with a surface of
332.73 ha, 47.6 ha, 37.65 ha and 27.68 ha respectively. For their part, the natural formations
dominant correspond to the Teline monspessulana Shrubland, a native forest for the preservation of
Nothofagus obliqua, Teline monspessulana arborescent thicket and native forest of
preservation of Aextoxicon punctatum.
According to the field campaigns, the vascular flora recorded in the area of influence of the
Project accounts for the presence of 247 species, of which 167 develop independently.
natural or spontaneous in the national territory, distributed in 106 native and 61 endemic; and 80
They correspond to species introduced to the country. Regarding the 61 endemic species, none is
regional endemic. According to growth habit, the greatest number of species
identified in the area of influence correspond to herbs (annual and perennial) with 145 taxa,
followed by shrubs (65 species) and trees (37 species).
19 species were registered under conservation category in the area of ​​influence of the Project. Of
total of registered species, five (5) are threatened, corresponding to
Gomortega keule, Pitavia punctata and Vestia foetida in the Endangered category, Asplenium trilobum and
Citronella mucronata in Vulnerable category. The remaining 14 taxa are
species not considered
in degree of threat27 (Near Threatened and Least Concern), corresponding to Gardoquia
multiflora and Polystichum subintegerrimum in the Near Threatened category; Adiantum chilense,
Aextoxicon punctatum, Asplenium dareoides, Blechnum arcuatum, Blechnum chilense, Blechnum
hastatum, Drimys winteri, Hymenophyllum dicranotrichum, Hypolepis poeppigii, Lophosoria
quadripinnata, Luma checken and Persea lingue of Least Concern.
27 The International Union for Conservation of Nature (IUCN) classifies these species into three
different categories on its Red List of Threatened Species: Vulnerable Species (VU), Endangered
extinction (EN) and Critically Endangered (CR), depending on the risk of extinction they are at
subjected.

national. However, the Project does not contemplate its intervention or the alteration of its

Negatives would be presented for Gomortega keule and Gardoquia multiflora, since both

species in a historical period (1980-2010) and in the future period (2035-2065), which gives
account of the existence of climatic conditions conducive to the existence of the species.
The above should not be interpreted as a change in the density or range of
geographical distribution of these species.
• The presence of three (3) species regulated by special protection measures was recorded,
corresponding to Gomortega keule, Pitavia punctata and Lapageria rosea.
• The presence of 61 endemic species was recorded in the area of ​​influence.

To calculate the environmental relevance of vegetation, the following criteria were used:
Abundance (Ab), Rarity (Ra), Fragility (Fr) and Diversity (Di), averaging these.
Below is the definition of the criteria used.
Abundance (Ab)
This criterion is related to the surface of the vegetation formation in relation to the surface
of the sub-use of land to which it corresponds, within the area of Influence. Your score will be higher
when the surface of the vegetation formation is of a smaller proportion.

b) Environmental relevance of flora
The environmental relevance for the flora described in the area of influence, and that will be affected by the
construction of the Project, is estimated based on the results presented in the Baseline
of the component, considering the registered environmental singularities and the information
recorded at the ground sampling points.
To calculate the environmental relevance of vegetation, the following criteria were used:
Abundance (Ab), Rarity (Ra), Fragility (Fr), Significance (Si) and Conservation Difficulty (Dc),
averaging these.

Below is the definition of the criteria used.
Abundance (Ab)
This criterion is related to the frequency of the species in relation to the total points of
sampling carried out within the area of influence. Your score will be higher when the frequency of the
species is low.
Table 4-100. Abundance criterion for the flora to intervene
Abundance Score (Ab)
10 < 5%
7- 9 5 - 25%
4 - 6 25 - 50%
1 - 3 > 50%
Source: GAC
Rarity (Ra)
This criterion is related to the phytogeographic origin of the species.
Table 4-101. Rarity criterion for the flora to intervene
Rarity Score (Ra)
10 Regional endemic
7 – 9 National endemic
4 - 6 Native
1 - 3 Introduced
Source: GAC
Fragility (Fr)
This criterion is related to the species' susceptibility to climate change.
Table 4-102. Fragility criterion for the flora to intervene
Fragility Score (Fr)
10 High susceptibility
7-9 Moderate susceptibility
4-6 Mild susceptibility
1-3 No susceptibility
Source: GAC
Significance (Sig)
This criterion is related to whether the species is considered a natural monument.

ii. Identified Impacts
a) IFV-01: Loss of vegetation formations
Construction Phase
The construction and implementation of the parts, works and actions of the Project implies the
intervention of surfaces for the leveling and preparation of land, with a series of
activities, among which we can mention earthworks and escarpments, which
involve cutting, clearing or loss of vegetation activities.
The works with the greatest surface occupation correspond to Extraction Zones (ZE) and Production Zones.
Disposition (ZD). In general, both these works and the majority of the works associated with the Project
require an initial escarpment or earth movement, which involves previously cutting the vegetation
existing there. Regarding the latter, the cutting of vegetation will occur to the extent that
progress in each of the works.
During the construction phase, the works in which the cutting of vegetation will be carried out
correspond to ZD Neptuno, ZE Victoria Norte, ZE Luna, existing roads with modification,
projected roads, Processing Plant, temporary topsoil collection area (ZAV) and
LTE Intervention Area.

LTE Intervention Area.

endemic and introduced flora recorded in the vegetation formations that will be seen
intervened in the area of influence of the Project.
The impact of the loss of specimens of
flora in the construction phase manifests itself in the area
directly from the site of the Project works, specifically due to clearance activities
of the vegetation in the natural and intervened environments that will be carried out for the materialization
of the planned works. In this way, the Project estimates that during the construction phase
113.55 hectares of vegetation formations will be involved and, therefore, their floristic composition and
isolated specimens of flora.

a series of activities, among which we can mention earthworks and escarpments,
those that involve cutting, clearing or loss of vegetation activities.

iii. Importance of impacts
a) IFV-01 Loss of vegetation formations
Construction Phase
The loss of vegetation cover corresponds to a Negative Character (Ca=-1), since a
deterioration of the basal condition of the factor. The Magnitude (Mag=12) of the projection of the works
is maximum or total, given that the loss of vegetation formations will be complete in the
sectors where the Project works will be built. For its part, the Extension is considered as
punctual (Ex=1), since the impact manifests itself in the sector where the work of the
Project. The Duration (Du=2) is considered temporary or transitory because the permanence of
The project works will be between 1 and 10 years, the Reversibility of the effect is taken as Irreversible
(Re=4), since it is considered that at this stage the impact is not reversed in a period shorter than the
15 years. The Synergy factor to climate change (SiCC=1) was considered with a simple synergism, the
Synergy/Accumulation with other projects (Yes/AcOp=1) resulted in slightly Synergistic. with
Regarding Periodicity, the effect is classified as Continuous (Pr=4), since the construction
contemplates the total clearance of vegetation.
According to the above, the importance of this impact corresponds to -5.8.

construction of the project. The Duration (Du=2) is considered temporary or transitory because the
permanence of the project works will be between 1 and 10 removing all individuals from
flora present, in the same way the Reversibility of the effect is taken as Irreversible (Re=4),
since it is considered that in this phase the impact is not reversed in a period of less than 15 years.
The Synergy factor to climate change (SiCC=4) was considered very synergistic with climate change,
Synergy/Accumulation with other projects (Si/AcOp=1) resulted in slightly Synergistic. with
Regarding Periodicity, the effect is classified as Continuous (Pr=4), since the construction
contemplates the total clearance of vegetation.
According to the above, the importance of this impact corresponds to -6.1.

Operation Phase

during the operation phase will cause direct intervention and, therefore, the loss of species

observes a deterioration of the basal condition of the factor. The magnitude of the projection of the works
is maximum or total (Mag=12), given that the loss of flora individuals will be total in the
sectors where the Project works will be built. For its part, the Extension is considered as
punctual (Ex=1), since the loss of flora specimens will be in the sectors where the
construction of the project. The Duration (Du=2) is considered temporary or transitory because the

flora present, in the same way the Reversibility of the effect is taken as Irreversible (Re=4),

4.3.3.8 Fauna (wild animals)
i. Environmental relevance vertebrate fauna
To quantify and qualify the impacts on vertebrate fauna, we first proceeded to assess
the environmental relevance of the fauna species of interest29 and/or sensitive30 for the Project, as well as
as well as the registered sites of interest. Information on these defined species is
obtained from the Wild Animal Baseline and the complementary studies included in the
Chapter 3 of this EIA.
This was how, for the fauna species of interest and/or sensitive, the environmental relevance was calculated
averaging the following criteria: rarity (Ra), abundance (Ab), significance (Si) and fragility (Fr);
assigning a higher weight to this last criterion with respect to the rest of the criteria.
In order to clarify the weighting given, the definition of
the criteria considered for the species of interest and/or sensitive, and then the assessment is delivered
granted for each species. Subsequently, and in the same order, the information on the
identified sites of interest.
a) Relevance criteria for fauna species of interest and/or sensitive
• Rarity
This criterion is related to the biogeographic origin of the species to be evaluated, being higher in the
as the species is native to the country.
