To define climate risk at the species level, ARCLIM uses the final database of
occurrences, extracting current and future values of temperature climate parameters
average and annual precipitation by species. In this way, models are made using ARCLIM
or the Maxent R software tool, for species classified as threatened and/or
those that, under expert criteria, merit evaluation. These species correspond to:

(Near Threatened) and Puma concolor (Near Threatened). The species selection criterion does not obey
only to classification categories, but also to the sensitivity of the species in relation to
natural characteristics such as the degree of mobility, ecosystem role and potential interaction with
the project among other factors.

ii. Identified Impacts
a) IFA-01 Loss of specimens of fauna of interest and/or sensitive.
The present impact may occur for all three phases of the Project (Construction, Operation and
Closing).
b) IFA-02 Loss and/or modification of habitat of species of interest and/or sensitive.
It corresponds to the significant modification of the conditions and resources necessary for the
existence of native species, as a consequence of the total removal of the soil and its vegetation
4-160
==================================================================================
PAGE 170
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
and/or changes in the places they travel. The concept of habitat is usually used to refer to a
sector of space that meets certain conditions that allow the existence of some species,
but not from others.
It is important to highlight that this impact includes in its evaluation the fragmentation of
natural environments and habitats as a result of the removal of vegetation and earthworks, which
which makes the movement of fauna species difficult (especially low-mobility species),
affects genetic variability and reduces the ability of vertebrates to search for food
larger terrestrials.
iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) IFA-01 Loss of specimens of fauna of interest and/or sensitive.
Construction Phase
Subfactor: Amphibians and reptiles
For amphibians and reptiles, the “Loss of specimens of fauna of interest and/or sensitive” is
negative character (Ca=-1) since it implies a deterioration of the basal condition, because during
This phase contemplates the installation of works and the development of activities in the sectors where
species belonging to this group are recorded and inhabited, being subject to the risk of
crushing. The magnitude is maximum (Mag=12) considering that the basal condition changes
drastically generating the death of individuals with low mobility capacity. The
extension is partial (Ex=2) since the loss of specimens will manifest in the environment
immediately to intervene within the area of influence of the Project. The persistence or duration is
permanent (Du=2) since the loss of individuals cannot be corrected and, therefore, is
irreversible (Re=4). It is considered that there is a moderate synergy with climate change
(SiCC=2) since there is a moderate risk to the species regarding climate change. The project is
synergistic with other projects (Si/AcOp=4) since it starts from the surface of the area of influence
interacts with other projects that have RCA. The periodicity (Pr=4) is continuous, due to
that the loss of specimens would manifest itself throughout the construction phase, which keeps
relationship with the activity of machinery in natural environments.

basal condition is considerable. The extension is punctual (Ex=1) since during this phase the

Closing Phase
Subfactor: Amphibians and reptiles
For amphibians and reptiles, the “Loss of specimens of fauna of interest and/or sensitive” is
negative character (Ca=-1), since it implies a deterioration of the basal condition. The magnitude is low
(Mag=1) since the basal condition changes at a minimum level. The extension is punctual (Ex=1)
since it is associated with the sector where the source is located. The duration of this impact
is constant (Du=2) since the loss of individuals is permanent. The impact is irreversible (Re=4)
since the resource cannot be restored by natural means in the affected areas. The impact
has a moderate synergy with climate change (SiCC=2) since it is considered a risk level
medium. The project is synergistic with other projects (Si/AcOp=4) since part of the surface of the
area of influence interacts with other projects that have RCA. The periodicity is irregular
(Pr=1) since the impact would be generated sporadically, exceptionally during the closing phase of the Project.

4.3.3.9 Invertebrate Fauna
i. Environmental relevance invertebrate fauna
The community of invertebrates present in the area of influence of the project for the period of
summer (2023) is made up of a total of 141 species. Of all of them, the
presence of the insecta class, Entognatha class and Arachnida class. For the Insecta Class,
1686 individuals, 35 individuals for the Entognatha class and 34 individuals for the Arachnida class. The
abundance of insects is concentrated with the presence of the order Coleoptera with 776 individuals,
grouped into 22 families and 47 species.
For the campaign carried out in winter (2023), a total of 1,324 were prospected.
individuals that includes 160 species. Species of the classes Insecta, Diplopoda,
Archnida, Collembola, Chilopoda and Malacostraxa. The Insecta Class dominates the assembly with 71%
with respect to the other classes. For insecta, 946 individuals were observed, entognatha 153 individuals, and
Class Arachnida 169 individuals.
Of the total number of species recorded during the summer and winter campaign, 4 present states of
conservation according to the RCE:

Species Conservation category Decree

Phrixotrichus scrofa Endangered (EN) DS 44/2021 MMA
Source: GAC
The Environmental Relevance (Ra) for the species of interest and/or sensitive is established based on the
average of a series of attributes studied in the Baseline that determine its quality or
condition of importance and significance, and by the expert judgment of the specialist that is based on the
experience acquired in your field.

extension is maximum or total (Ex=8), since the loss of copies will manifest itself in the

The surface of the area of influence interacts with other projects that have RCA. The

4.3.3.10 Continental Aquatic Ecosystems
i. Environmental relevance Continental Aquatic Ecosystems
For the installation of the project, the execution of works with the potential to modify
any of the attributes of the aquatic ecosystems present in the area of influence, due to
which considers the implementation of works of art that will require the diversion of waters from the section
to intervene through a by-pass channel (in the event that one of the channels encounters
runoff at the time of implementation of the work). In this section the
civil works planned for each work (installation of tubes and/or prefabricated caissons, bridges or
layout modification as applicable) which will be made of concrete or corrugated steel.
4-188
==================================================================================
PAGE 198
==================================================================================
Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of
Rare Earth Concentrate
In the specific case of crossing channels, the area where it does not intervene will be excavated (without
interaction with the channel), that is, dry excavation, and connections are made with closures or
cofferdams; Subsequently, compacted fill from the rolling folder is applied. Finally
generate the necessary work to return the watercourse to its natural channel (for both
cases, traversals or modifications). While modifications or interventions in channels
Natural areas with continuous water runoff are usually executed through excavations with
machines, preferably using excavators with long arms and medium to large buckets.
volume, which proceeds to divert the normal flow of water, maintaining the flow and in this way
way to allow the execution of works of art, without total interference from the flow of water.
Consequently, this evaluation assumes that the construction of permanent works and
The temporary effects of the Project will have the potential to affect, in a limited way, bodies of water
indicated above, specifically will have the potential to generate differential effects
on the quality of the waters present in the projected crossings, as well as the potential to alter
portions of the habitat of those species in conservation category. This prediction is made
for those crossings of channels that will be carried out through an open ditch, which may
generate resuspension of settleable solids, possibly modifying the conditions
physical properties of the water, having a local impact on its state variables (pH and dissolved oxygen),
as well as the physical characteristics that
configure the habitat of species in the category of
conservation.
Specifically, the works and layout of the project will cross limited sections of estuaries and streams.
which are detailed below:
1. Estero Penco
2. Permanent streams
The basal characteristics of the bodies of water present in the area of influence are found
described in Chapter 3 of the “Baseline”, Section B, where the existence of
bodies of water of natural origin. The above suggests that in certain sectors (e.g. stations
PE, P7, P9 and P10) could be sharing certain characteristics of the water column, as well as
their biological communities. The physical parameters quantified in situ do not show the presence
of foreign bodies and/or remains of hydrocarbons in the system. Temperature, oxygen values
dissolved, conductivity and pH quantified are as expected and are within the ranges
regulated in NCh 1,333.
Throughout the area of influence, it was evident that the quality of the surface water meets the
requirements established in the reference standard (NCh 1.333 of.78), with the exception of some
specific stations (e.g. P18 and P23) where iron and manganese exceeded the norm, of the same

water when there is an increase in the flow of water bodies.
From the biological perspective, the continental aquatic ecosystems of the area of influence
showed the presence of a maximum richness of 16 taxa of phytobenthic cells in the campaign
winter, where the species Cymbella cistula stood out, present in all seasons of
sampling. The phytoplankton was characterized by a maximum richness of 12 cell taxa
phytoplankton, with the greatest abundance and representativeness the genus Navicula sp., with
average abundances of 251.66 cell/L. On the other hand, zooplankton recorded the maximum presence
of 5 taxa identified, with the larvae of the family Chironomidae (Diptera) being the most
representative and abundant.

the catfish Trichomycterus areolatus being the most abundant species, with 12 specimens in total
for the 2022 winter campaign and 8 specimens for the 2023 summer campaign (Table 4-156).

Regarding the habitat preferences of the species in the threatened category that inhabit the
area of influence, it is indicated that specimens of T. aerolatus inhabit rhythron-type environments, their
Juveniles are preferably distributed in shallow coastal areas with muddy bottoms.
and little vegetation. While adult specimens are distributed in the dead zone of the
channels, up to 40 cm deep and current speeds of up to 3 m/s (Arratia 198332).
While specimens of the genus Aeglas inhabit shallow and lentic rheophilic environments with
good environmental conditions and relatively well oxygenated waters and depend directly or
indirectly from the contributions of organic matter from the native riparian vegetation,

Therefore, they have been considered sensitive organisms to environmental disturbances of their
habitat (Trevisan et al., 200933, Catchpole et al., 202134).
The species in conservation status reported in the area of influence are sensitive to the
changes occurred in its environment, evidencing that the recovery or restoration of the
Aquatic biotic communities are dynamic, with a differential succession pattern existing
depending on the type of species (Vivas et al., 200235). Specifically, the responses of the
fish communities in Chile to the alterations of their habitats have been little studied, without
However, there is evidence of a rapid recovery of the intervened habitats and a rapid
colonization by resilient species after the recovery of disturbed habitats,
probably as a consequence of the species' capacity for movement or vagility
of fish, as well as the recovery of its associated biota (macroinvertebrates) (Soto et
al. 2006, Habit et al. 2007). In this context, and given the characteristics of the Project and its
interactions with the surface water bodies present in the area of influence, is that
They expect modifications in limited portions of the environments defined as habitat of species
of fish fauna and decapods in conservation category, specifically sections of the estuary
Penco where channel crossings can be seen. In no case does the Project contemplate the
total alteration of the distribution habitat of this species, as well as the introduction of
substances exogenous to these environments. Additionally, refunds of the
physical characteristics that define
these environments, which will allow the repopulation of the areas
disturbed once the planned interventions are completed.
As mentioned previously, the surface water network in the area of influence of the Project
It is made up of several bodies of water of natural origin. Additionally, bodies of water
characterized recorded the presence of 1 species of fish of native origin: Trichomycterus
areolatus (Vulnerable), as well as species of decapod crustaceans. Consequently, due to the
importance of surface waters for the establishment of fish fauna and species of
crustaceans of native origin, a High environmental relevance value (7) is assigned for this
component.

ii. Identified Impacts
a) IEA-01 Alteration in the quality of surface waters
b) IEA-02 Habitat alteration of species in conservation category
In this evaluation it is assumed that the construction of the permanent and temporary works of the
Project will have the potential to affect surface water bodies associated with the area of the
project, specifically will have the potential to generate differential effects on the quality of
the waters present in the projected crossings, as well as the potential to alter limited portions
of the habitat of those species in the conservation category that inhabit the water courses
modify, with emphasis on the Penco estuary, where the highest abundance of species was reported in
conservation category. Specifically, this prediction is proposed for those crossings of
channels that will be made through an open ditch, which may generate resuspension of solids
sedimentable, potentially modifying the physical conditions of the waters,
impacting locally on its state variables.
iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) IEA-01 Alteration in the quality of surface waters
Construction Phase
The nature of the impact is considered negative (Ca=-1) since during the construction phase
will carry out works and excavations for the installation of works of art that will have the potential to
modify the state variables that describe the quality of the waters. Mainly as
consequence of the resuspension of settleable solids, which may modify the conditions
physical characteristics of water such as turbidity, locally affecting state variables (pH,
temperature and dissolved oxygen). The magnitude of the impact is low (Mag=1) because the eventual
detriment to the quality of the water would be associated only with its physicochemical condition,
particularly, to the resuspension of settleable solids, modifying the physical conditions of
the waters. And it does not imply the introduction of polluting substances to bodies of water. The
extension will be partial (Ex=2), because the effect of sediment resuspension will manifest
in the immediate surroundings of the works, with dilution downstream of the sectors where it is projected
the implementation of works of art. The duration will be punctual (Du=1), since the impact will occur
during the construction phase of the Project. Specifically as a consequence of the activities
related to the construction of crossings and channel diversions. The impact is considered
reversible in the short term (Re=1), since once the works that involve the resuspension of
sediments, the physicochemical quality of the water and sediments will regain their natural properties
basal. It is not considered
ra the existence of synergy with climate change (SiCC=1). The accumulation

alteration or modification of the channel, these sectors will be available to be recolonized by

4.3.3.11 Archeology
An alteration of archaeological finds will occur, therefore, the impact must be evaluated
of the Project on the object of protection of Archaeological Monuments.
According to the results of the visual archaeological inspection carried out inside the area
of the Project, an inspection coverage of 43.09% of the total surface of the AI of
Archeology (70.72 ha of the total 164.09 ha), through transects separated every 20m from each other.
From the inspection carried out, only one archaeological site was recognized, called PMP-
SA-01, corresponding to a concentration of ceramic fragments from smoothed surfaces
(interior and exterior) of 146 m2, of possible historical temporality of indigenous tradition (judging by
the presence of fragments of smoothed surfaces, without lathe marks and with the use of antiplastics

climate.

uncommon.

climate change (SiCC=1), due to the risk of loss of vegetation formations and
loss of greenery in native forests (biophysical attribute of the landscape) is slight38. There is a
Synergy/accumulation with other projects in an important way as a result of its relationship with
other projects, such as the Cemarc landfill and the presence of extensive plantations
forests, which include recently harvested sectors (devoid of vegetation) (Yes/A-
OP=4). The periodicity is Continuous (Pr=4), since the alteration on the biophysical attributes, in
particular in the vegetation, will be presented constantly throughout the entire phase of
construction.

4.3.3.13 Territory Use-Road Infrastructure
i. Environmental relevance Land Use-Road Infrastructure
The Project is located mainly in the commune of Penco and some sectors in the extreme north
from the commune of Concepción, Biobío Region. For access from/to public roads,
Consider using two accesses:
• Access 1 - Route 150 Km 5, Route Penco - Lirquén.
• Access 2 - Route 152 Km 71 Itata Route.
Access from route 152 will allow entry to the Processing Plant from public roads
existing and then from there connect to the different areas of the Project through the use of
internal roads. On the other hand, the existing access on route 150 will allow direct entry
both to the processing plant and to the extraction and disposal areas of the Project.
To reach the aforementioned accesses, it is necessary to use the aforementioned routes Route 150 and Route
152, complementary to these routes, and to connect with points of origin or destination of actions of
transportation to be generated by the Project, other access routes are required, such as the Route
154, Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri, Av. Costanera, Av. El Manzano, among others, which will allow
connect with the main sources of inputs, personnel, waste destination, as well as points
transportation for the processed mineral (Puerto de Lirquén).

Chapter 4
Prediction and Evaluation of Environmental Impacts
EIA Mining Development Project for Clay Extraction for Production of

Figure 4-21. Access roads
Source: GAC
The Area of Influence was defined considering the public routes that connect the Project with each
one of the origins and destinations of the trips generated and attracted by it, considering the different
transportation actions, the above taking into account the Area of Influence Guide in the SEIA,
Exempt Resolution No. 423 of the Executive Directorate of the SEA (2017).
In particular, the roads that make up the Area of Influence and that allow access to the different
areas of this correspond to the following:
• Route 150, between Av. El Manzano and Route 154.
• Route 152, between Route 150 and Los Coihues Underpass.
• Av. El Manzano, between Route 150 and Puerto Lirquén Access.
• Access road to Puerto Lirquén, between Av. Manzano and the checkpoint.
• Route 154, between Route 150 and Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez.
• Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez, between Route 154 and Av. Costanera.
• Av. Costanera, between Av. Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez and Av. Great Britain.

The public roads mentioned
correspond to the most viable alternatives for access to the Project,
because they allow connection with the points of origin of necessary transport activities or with
the structuring road of the region that allows its access; and because they have a standard
operation that enables the transit of the Project's heavy vehicles, without major interference.
Likewise, the increase in vehicle demand generated by the Project, due to the transfer of
inputs, personnel, equipment and finished products, necessary in the different phases of this,
could affect the travel times of road users in the area of influence.
The above indicates that the Environmental Relevance of the Road Infrastructure element of the component
Territory Use is considered High (7).
This evaluation is carried out based on the information presented in Annex 4-3, where
The potential externalities of the execution of the Project on the local road network have been analyzed,

considering restrictive vehicle concentration criteria for both the Project (temporary cut and

ii. Identified Impacts
a) IEV-01 Alteration of travel times of users of public routes
access to the project
Construction Phase
During the construction phase of the Project, the use of routes in the road influence area is expected.
of this, mainly routes 150, 152, 154, Pdte. Jorge Alessandri Rodríguez and Av. Costanera,
this for the transfer of supplies, machinery, personnel, equipment and waste necessary for the
phase development.
In order to quantify the consumption of resources that the Project could exert on the
adjacent public roads, is that in the Road Impact Study (Annex 4-3) two
analysis, the first considered the modeling of the relevant intersections through the software
SIDRA and the second was an analysis of the Level of Service in the road sections of the area of influence.
Intersection modeling allows quantifying the incidence of vehicular flow generated by
the Project in terms of indicators such as saturation, queue length and average delay in the
intersections relevant to transportation activity; For its part, the Service Level analysis
allows categorizing the operation of road sections based on factors such as speed, time
of travel, operational costs, freedom of maneuvers, among others, in accordance with the provisions
in the Highway Manual (MOP 2023). The objective of both exercises was to identify if the
incorporation of the Project flow, in a restrictive condition, will generate an affectation
significant in the indicated parameters, and as a consequence a significant increase in the
travel times of public road users.
The modeled intersections were the following:
• PM N°1: Av. El Manzano/ Av. La Marina.
• PM N°2: Av. El Manzano/ Route 150 access branch:
o PM N°2-1: Puerto Lirquén Winery Access/ Route 150 access branch.
o PM N°2-2: Av. El Manzano/ Route 150 access branch.
• PM N°3: Route 150/Puerto Lirquén access branch:
o PM N°3-1: Route 150 with Puerto Lirquén access branch (Eastern access).
o PM N°3-2: Route 150 with Puerto Lirquén access branch (west access).

that, the incorporation of the Project flow does not generate a variation in the indicator. It is also indicated
that the rest of the intersections are below the practical saturation threshold (85%) and the
The Project's vehicle contribution does not generate variation or is marginal, compared to the baseline scenario.

iii. Importance of identified impacts
a) IEV-01 Alteration of travel times of users of public routes
access to the project
Construction Phase
This impact has been classified as Negative in nature (Ca=-1), because during the
construction will generate flows of light vehicles
and heavy from/to the Project, which
will imply an increase in vehicular flow due to the transportation of supplies, machinery, equipment,
waste and personnel. The Magnitude is considered medium (Mag=2), because the increase in flow
vehicle implies changes in the basal condition but within acceptable ranges, according to
the results obtained in the road modeling and service level analysis, carried out in the Annex
4-3 (Road Impact Study). The extent of the impact is identified as broad (Ex=3), since it
effects occur outside the immediate environment of the source that generates it and in different sectors
of the area of influence. It is considered a temporary or transitory Duration (Du=2), because the
Vehicular flow will be developed during the construction phase, with an extension of 25 months. Given
that the effect on road flows will be reversed by natural means, once the phase of
construction, the effect is considered Reversible in the short term (Re=1). The impact is
considered without Synergism with Climate Change because the evaluation is carried out in accordance with
the current condition of the component and not according to its possible evaluation under scenarios of
climate change (SiCC=0). Regarding Synergy/Accumulation with other projects (Yes/A-OP=1), it is
considers that it is slightly synergistic/cumulative, since there is another project, the magnitude,
joint duration and extension does not modify the effect of the project alone. Periodicity is
intermittent (Pr=2) since the alteration of the displacement dynamics will manifest itself with a certain
periodicity during the construction phase. With the above, the Importance (I) of the impact increases
to -2.2.

4.3.3.14 Human Environment
i. Human environment environmental relevance
According to what is stated in the Characterization of the Human Environment, the Project is located 2 km
approximated to the East of the city of Penco, while in the rural context, there are some
plots with isolated homes in the vicinity of the works, specifically adjacent to the Landfill
Cemarc Sanitary (Las Encinas and Santa Matilde plots, 180 and 165 m away
respectively), homes were also identified in the sectors of El Cabrito and Los Varones
located respectively 1.5 km and 1.7 km northeast of the Victoria North ZE, both around the
route O-390.

Regarding indigenous human groups, there are spaces for common use specifically
around the Penco estuary, in which the development of traditional activities was identified, being
These spaces are areas close to the Project site.
According to the secondary information collected, and the information collected in studies
previous, some local inhabitants linked to the identified GHPPI, access the sectors of
edge of the Penco estuary in order to collect medicinal herbs. In this regard, there are in the city
of Penco two (2) urban Mapuche organizations that carry out cultural practices in the vicinity
of the Project, specifically those called “Lawen Mawida” and “Koñintu Lafken Mapu Penco”41.
The members of the first organization travel an existing private forest road and
adjacent to the Penco estuary up to km 1.2, where they carry out identification and collection workshops
of native and medicinal plants, a place located approximately 600 meters from the work
nearest (Victoria North extraction area). The members of the second of the organizations
indicated also use the same path, performing ceremonies linked to the collection of
herbs in the El Pozón sectors, located 529 meters from the nearest work; Jinolu Well, located
approximately 396 meters from the nearest work (Victoria Norte extraction area); The E
school,
located approximately 120 meters away. from the ZE Victoria Norte and Los Queules, approximately 280 meters from the
north of the nearest work (Victoria North extraction area); and also collecting herbs
medicinal products in the spring-summer season and raw materials for the production of basketry
Mapuche.
On the other hand, the areas near the Penco estuary are also used by local inhabitants
(non-indigenous human groups) for recreational and sporting purposes (presence of cyclists, runners
and hikers) and cultural-educational (development of educational activities Penco School).

cultural, for the socialization of the use of the medicinal herbs they collect, as well as the

Mawida, its main cultural practices are related to meetings, workshops to reactivate
the Mapuche language, the use of medicinal herbs and participation in ceremonial activities of
indigenous character.
Likewise, this Association expresses that the valorization of natural resources covers the entire
existing nature in the commune of Penco, that is, the mountains, hills, the coastal edge and the area
maritime, as unlike the Group, its connection with the environment is the first section
of the forest road. Identifying various sites of cultural significance such as La Cata Beach, the
nguillatuwe and the Menoko, being El Pozón, Pozo Jinolu, La Escuela and Los Queules, the sites in common
of cultural significance of both organizations, where they mainly carry out the collection of
medicinal herbs.
